صاحبین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قرضدار پر ان فلوس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی جو رواج کے بعد ٹھپ ہو گئے ہیں اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب فلوس کے ثمن ہونے کا وصف باطل ہو گیا تو ایسے فلوس کا واپس کرنا مستعد رہو گیا جیسے فلوس پر قبضہ کیا تھا کیونکہ جو فلوس شمن ہونے سے خالی ہیں وہ
And if he borrowed current fulus and they became demonetized, according to Abu Hanifa, he must return the like (mithl) of them because a loan is an 'ariyah (loan for use) and its requirement is to return the specific thing in meaning, and thaman status is an extra attribute in it because a loan is not specific to thaman. According to the two (Sahibayn), he must pay their value because when the attribute of thaman ceases, returning them as they were received becomes impossible, so their value must be returned, just as if someone borrowed a mithli (fungible) thing and it became unavailable (inquita'a). But according to Abu Yusuf, it is the value on the day of possession, and according to Muhammad, it is the value on the day of demonetization, as passed before. The origin of the difference is in the issue of someone who usurped a mithli thing and it became unavailable. The statement of Muhammad is fairer to both sides, and the statement of Abu Yusuf is easier. Translation: And if he borrowed current fulus, then their circulation stopped, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is obligatory for the borrower to return their like. Because taking a loan is an 'ariyah (loan for use) and its ruling is that the thing itself is returned in meaning, and thaman status is an extra attribute in it because a loan is not specific to thaman. And according to the Sahibayn, the borrower must pay their value. Explanation of the issue: A person borrowed current fulus, then their circulation and usage stopped. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is obligatory for the borrower to return their like, i.e., count and return the same number as he took. The proof is that borrowing a mithli thing is called 'ariyah, just as giving a mithli thing as a loan is called qard. And the ruling of borrowing a mithli thing is that it is returned in meaning, not in actuality. If we look at it as 'ariyah, then actually returning the specific thing should be obligatory because in 'ariyah, the same thing taken is returned. But since this is a loan, and in a loan the specific thing is consumed for benefit, therefore actually returning the specific thing becomes impossible. And when actually returning the specific thing becomes impossible, then returning it in meaning becomes obligatory, and returning in meaning can be done through the like. Therefore the borrower is obligated to return the like of the fulus. But note that this like is given the status of the actual thing, because if the like is not given the status of the actual thing, then the exchange of a thing for its kind with deferment (nasī'ah) would necessarily occur, which is impermissible. Therefore the like is given the status of the actual thing. 'And thaman status is an extra attribute in it...' etc. is an answer to a question. Question: How can the like of fulus be in the meaning of the actual thing? Because when the borrower took the fulus, they were thaman due to being current, but when he returns them after circulation has stopped, they are not thaman. So the non-current fulus are not the meaning-like of current fulus. So if he gives non-current fulus, it is not returning the like of what he took? Answer: The answer is that thaman status is an extra attribute in a loan because a loan is not specific to thaman. So when a loan is not specific to thaman, it will be said that borrowing fulus is based on them being among mithliyyat (fungibles), and the cessation of their circulation does not remove them from being mithliyyat. The upshot: The borrower borrowed a mithli thing and returned its like, i.e., the same number as he took, and by doing so the debt is discharged. Therefore according to Imam A'zam, paying the like discharges the debt. The school of the Sahibayn is that the borrower must pay the value of those fulus that became demonetized after circulation, and their proof is that when the attribute of thaman of fulus becomes void, returning them as they were received becomes impossible, because fulus devoid of thaman status are... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This extensive passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a loan (qard) of fulus that later become demonetized. The issue is whether the borrower must repay in kind (like) or in value. Abu Hanifa holds that the borrower must return the like (mithl) — the same number of fulus — because a loan is essentially an 'ariyah (loan for use) in meaning, and the thaman status is an incidental attribute. Since fulus are mithliyyat (fungibles), returning their like suffices even if they are no longer current. The Sahibayn argue that once fulus lose their thaman status, returning them as such is impossible, so the borrower must pay their value. Between the two, Abu Yusuf values at the time of possession, Muhammad at the time of demonetization. The text then addresses a potential objection: how can non-current fulus be the 'like' of current fulus? The answer is that the thaman status is not integral to the loan; fulus are mithliyyat regardless of currency. Therefore, returning the same quantity is valid. The passage also analogizes this to a case of usurpation (ghasb) of a mithli thing that becomes unavailable. The commentary emphasizes that the dispute centers on the nature of fulus as thaman or as mithliyyat, and the practical consequence is whether the borrower pays coins or cash value.

Key Terms
قرض (qard): Loan of fungible property (mithli) where the borrower consumes and returns the like (mithl).
مثلي (mithli): Fungible property that has standard units (like grains, coins, fulus) and can be replaced by the same quantity and quality.
ثمنية (thamanīyah): The attribute of being thaman (currency/medium of exchange). In this passage, fulus have thamanīyah when they are current (legal tender).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding a loan of fulus that later become demonetized?
A) The borrower must pay the value of the fulus at the time of the loan.
B) The borrower must return the like (mithl) of the fulus — the same number.
C) The loan is void because the fulus are no longer currency.
D) The borrower must pay the value at the time of demonetization.

Key Takeaway
In a loan of fulus, the Hanafi imams differ on whether repayment is in kind or in value when demonetization occurs; the choice depends on whether thaman status is considered essential to the loan.

8 min
Repayment of Loan When Currency Becomes Invalid: Hanafi Internal Dispute
Ruling with ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on repaying a loan of fulus after demonetization and identify the practical difference between mithl and qimat in this context.

Core Idea
Loan of fulus: if demonetized, Abu Hanifa says return same quantity; Abu Yusuf says value at possession; Muhammad says value at demonetization.

In this lesson, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: if someone borrows copper coins (fulus) that later lose their status as currency, what must they repay? The Great Imam, Abu Hanifa, insists on returning the same quantity (mithl), while his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue that value (qimat) must be paid. Even between the students, there is disagreement on which date to use for valuation. This passage from the Hidayah commentary walks through the proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the three positions
Understand the facts: a person borrows currently circulating fulus; then the fulus become demonetized. State what each imam says the debtor must return: Abu Hanifa: same quantity (mithl); Abu Yusuf: value on the day of possession; Muhammad: value on the day of demonetization.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the loan is of a mithli thing; the attribute of being currency is extraneous. Therefore, the debtor must return the same quantity, which is given the status of the actual thing to avoid exchanging a thing for its own kind on credit.
The key concept is that mithliyyat (fungibility) remains even after demonetization.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's proof (qiyas)
The Sahibayn analogize to a loan of wheat that disappears from the market: when mithl is impossible, value is wajib. Here, when the attribute of thaman is lost, returning the exact fulus is impossible, so value must be paid.
This qiyas is based on the idea that the loss of the thaman attribute makes mithl impossible.
4
Differentiate the two valuation dates
Abu Yusuf uses the day of possession (yawm al-qabd) because that is known and easy; Muhammad uses the day of demonetization (yawm al-inqita') to balance the interests of both lender and borrower.
The origin of this difference is a case of ghasb (usurpation) of a mithli thing.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author of Hidayah notes that Muhammad's view considers both parties, but Abu Yusuf's view is easier to apply because the price at possession is well-known. The passage suggests a preference for Abu Yusuf's view, but all three are recognized within the school.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is not explicitly stated; later practice may vary.

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے رائج الوقت فلوس کا قرضہ لیا پھر ان کا رواج اور چلن بند ہو گیا تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک قرضدار پر ان کی مثل واپس کرنا واجب ہے یعنی جس قدر فلوس لئے تھے گن کر اسی قدر واپس کر دے۔ دلیل یہ ہے مثلی چیز کا قرضہ لینا قرضہ کہلاتا ہے جیسا کہ مثلی چیز کو عاریہ دینا قرض کہلاتا ہے۔ اور مثلی چیز قرض لینے کا حکم یہ ہے کہ من حیث المعنی نہ کہ من حیث الحقیقت عین شئی کو واپس کیا جائے۔ اور اگر عاریہ ہونے پر نظر کی جائے تو حقیقت عین شئی کا واپس کرنا واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ عاریہ میں اسی چیز کو واپس کیا جاتا ہے جس کو لیا گیا تھا۔ لیکن چونکہ یہ قرض ہے اور قرض میں عین شئی کو تلف کر کے نفع حاصل کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے حقیقت عین شئی کا واپس کرنا ناممکن ہو گیا ہے اور جب حقیقت عین شئی کا واپس کرنا ناممکن ہو گیا تو معنی عین شئی کا واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا اور معنی میں شئی کی واپسی چونکہ مثل کے ذریعہ ہو سکتی ہے۔ اس لئے قرضدار پر فلوس کا مثل واجب کیا گیا ہے مگر یہ خیال رہے کہ اس مثل کو حقیقت عین شئی کا مرتبہ دیا جائے گا کیونکہ اگر مثل شئی کو حقیقت عین شئی کا مرتبہ نہ دیا گیا تو مبادلة الشئ بجنسه نسیئة لازم آئے گا حالانکہ یہ ناجائز ہے۔ اس لئے مثل شئی کو عین شئی کا درجہ دیا جائے گا۔
والثمنية فضل فيه..... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ یہاں فلوس کا مثل عین شئی کے معنی میں کیسے ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ جب قرضدار نے فلوس لئے تھے تو وہ رائج ہونے کی وجہ سے شمن تھے مگر جب رواج بند ہونے کے بعد ان کو واپس کرتا ہے تو اس وقت وہ شمن نہیں ہیں حاصل یہ کہ فلوس کا سدہ فلوس نافقہ کا معنی مثل نہیں ہیں اور جب فلوس کا سدہ فلوس نافقہ کا معنی مثل نہیں ہیں تو قرضدار کے فلوس کا سدہ ادا کرنے سے ان فلوس کا مثل ادا نہ ہو گا جن کو قرض لیا تھا؟
جواب: اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ شمن ہونا قرض میں ایک امر زائد ہے۔ کیونکہ قرض شمن کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے پس جب قرض شمن کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے تو یہ کہا جائے گا کہ فلوس کا قرضہ لینا ان کے ذوات الامثال میں سے ہونے کے اعتبار سے ہے اور فلوس کے چلن کا بند ہو جانا ان کو ذوات الامثال ہونے سے خارج نہیں کرتا حاصل یہ ہوا کہ قرضدار نے ایک مثلی چیز کو قرض لے کر اس کا مثل واپس کر دیا ہے یعنی جس قدر فلوس لئے تھے اس قدر واپس کر دیئے ہیں اور ایسا کرنے سے چونکہ قرضہ ادا ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے امام اعظم کے نزدیک فلوس کا مثل ادا کرنے سے قرضہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔
صاحبین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قرضدار پر ان فلوس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی جو رواج کے بعد ٹھپ ہو گئے ہیں اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب فلوس کے ثمن ہونے کا وصف باطل ہو گیا تو ایسے فلوس کا واپس کرنا متعذر ہو گیا جیسے فلوس پر قبضہ کیا تھا کیونکہ جو فلوس شمن ہونے سے خالی ہیں وہ ان کے معنی میں نہیں ہو سکتے جن میں وصف ثمنیت موجود ہے پس جب فلوس نافقہ جن کو قرضدار نے لیا تھا ان کے مثل کا واپس کرنا متعذر گیا تو ان کی قیمت واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ جیسے اگر کسی آدمی نے گندم وغیرہ مثلی چیز کو قرضہ کے طور پر لیا ہو اور پھر وہ بازار میں منقطع ہوگئی ہو تو اس کی قیمت کا واپس کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے ایسا ہی مذکورہ مسئلہ میں بھی قیمت واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ قاضی ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس دن کی قیمت ادا کرنا واجب ہوگا جس دن قرضدار نے ان پر قبضہ کیا تھا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس دن کی قیمت واجب ہوگی جس دن ان کا رواج اور چلن بند ہوا ہے۔ صاحبین کے درمیان اختلاف کی اصل اس مسئلہ میں ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے مثلی چیز کو غصب کیا پھر وہ منقطع ہو گئی تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یوم غصب کی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک یوم انقطاع کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد کے قول میں قرضہ دینے والے اور قرضہ لینے والے دونوں کی رعایت ہے۔ قرضہ دینے والے کی رعایت تو امام صاحب کے قول کے مقابلہ میں ہے کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ان فلوس کا مثل واجب ہوتا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس میں قرضہ دینے والے کی کوئی رعایت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مقرض تو فلوس نافقہ دے کر فلوس کا سدہ لے رہا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول کے مقابلہ میں قرضہ لینے والے کی رعایت ہے اس طور پر کہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک قرضہ لینے والے پر قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے اور جس دن قرضہ لینے والے نے فلوس پر قبضہ کیا تھا اس دن چونکہ وہ رائج اور چالو تھے اس لئے اس دن ان کی قیمت زیادہ ہو گی اور اس میں قرضہ لینے والے کی کوئی رعایت نہیں ہے۔ پس ظاہر ہوا کہ امام محمد کے قول میں مقروض اور مقرض دونوں کی رعایت پیش نظر ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے قول میں آسانی زیادہ ہے کیونکہ جس دن مستقرض نے قرضہ پر قبضہ کیا تھا اس دن کی قیمت مقرض، مستقرض اور تمام لوگوں کو معلوم ہے۔ لہذا اس پر عمل کرنا آسان ہے اور یوم انقطاع کی قیمت لوگوں پر مشتبہ ہوگی اور اس میں شدید اختلاف ہوگا۔ اس لئے یوم انقطاع کی قیمت معلوم کرنا اور اس پر شریعت کا حکم مرتب کرنا آسان نہیں ہے۔
Because when the attribute of being currency (thaman) becomes void, then returning the same coins (as taken) becomes impossible, so it is obligatory to return their value. For example, if someone took a loan of a thing of the same kind (mithli) and then that thing disappeared from the market. However, according to Abu Yusuf, the price on the day of possession is obligatory, and according to Imam Muhammad, the price on the day of demonetization is obligatory, as has passed before. The original difference is in the case of a person who usurped a mithli thing and then it disappeared. Imam Muhammad's saying takes care of both parties, and Imam Abu Yusuf's saying has more ease. Explanation: The scenario is that a person took a loan of currently circulating fulus; then their circulation stopped. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the debtor must return their mithl (like quantity). The proof is: Taking a loan of a mithli thing is called a loan, just as giving a mithli thing as ariyah (loan for use) is called a loan. The ruling of taking a loan of a mithli thing is that the exact thing is returned in meaning (meaning), not in reality. If it were seen as ariyah, returning the exact thing would be obligatory. But since it is a loan, and in a loan the exact thing is consumed for benefit, returning the exact thing is impossible. When returning the exact thing has become impossible, returning the thing in meaning becomes obligatory. Returning in meaning is possible through mithl, so the debtor is obliged to return the mithl of fulus. It should be noted that this mithl will be given the status of the actual thing. Otherwise, exchanging a thing for its own kind on credit would become necessary, which is impermissible. Therefore, the mithl is given the status of the actual thing. 'And the attribute of being thaman is extra...' etc. This is an answer to a question. The question is: How can the mithl of fulus be in the meaning of the actual thing? Because when the debtor took the fulus, they were currency due to being current, but when he returns them after demonetization, they are not currency. So the mithl of current fulus is not the mithl of non-current fulus. So paying the mithl of non-current fulus would not be the mithl of the fulus he took? Answer: The answer is that being currency (thaman) is an extra attribute in the loan. Because the loan is not specific to currency. So when the loan is not specific to currency, it will be said that taking a loan of fulus is based on them being from the category of mithliyyat (fungible goods). The cessation of circulation does not remove them from being mithliyyat. So the debtor took a mithli thing as a loan and returned its mithl, i.e., he returned as many fulus as he took. Since doing so fulfills the loan, according to the Great Imam, paying the mithl of fulus will fulfill the loan. The school of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the debtor must pay the value of those fulus that became demonetized. Their proof: When the attribute of being currency has become void, returning such fulus is impossible because the fulus taken were marketable. Since the fulus he took are mithli, but when their attribute of being thaman is lost, they cannot be the same in meaning. So it becomes impossible to return their mithl, so paying their value is obligatory. For example, if someone took a loan of wheat etc., and then that item disappeared from the market, paying its value is obligatory. Similarly, in this case, paying the value is obligatory. However, according to Qadi Abu Yusuf, it is obligatory to pay the value of the day when the debtor took possession; according to Imam Muhammad, the value of the day when they became demonetized. The origin of the difference between the two is in the case of a person who usurped a mithli thing, then it was lost. According to Abu Yusuf, the value on the day of usurpation is obligatory; according to Muhammad, the value on the day of loss. The author of Hidayah says: In Muhammad's saying, consideration is given to both the lender and the borrower. Consideration to the lender as opposed to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying, because in his saying, the mithl is obligatory, and obviously, there is no consideration for the lender. Because the lender gives current fulus and receives non-current fulus. And in opposition to Abu Yusuf's saying, there is consideration for the borrower: According to Abu Yusuf, the borrower must pay the price of the day of possession, and on that day the fulus were current, so their price would be high, and there is no consideration for the borrower. So it becomes clear that in Muhammad's saying, both the borrower and lender are considered. In Abu Yusuf's saying, there is more ease, because the price on the day of possession is known to the lender, borrower, and all people, so acting upon it is easy. The price on the day of demonetization would be doubtful, and there would be severe difference about it. So determining the price on the day of demonetization and applying the shari'ah ruling is not easy.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a loan of currency (fulus) that becomes demonetized after the borrower takes possession. The passage begins by stating the ruling of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) that when the attribute of being currency is lost, returning the same coins is impossible, so the value must be paid. It then provides a detailed explanation (tashrih) of the scenario. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the debtor must return the same quantity (mithl) of fulus, because the loan is of a mithli item, and by custom, mithl can substitute for the actual thing. The author defends Abu Hanifa's view by answering an objection: that after demonetization, the fulus are no longer currency, so how can they be the mithl? The answer is that being currency is an extraneous attribute; the loan is based on the items being mithliyyat, and demonetization does not remove them from that category. The Sahibayn argue that the mithl is impossible when the attribute of currency is lost, so value is obligatory. They analogize to a loan of wheat that disappears from the market. The passage then notes the further ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf requires value on the day of possession (yawm al-qabd), while Muhammad requires value on the day of demonetization (yawm al-inqita'). The origin of this difference is a case of ghasb (usurpation) of a mithli thing that is later lost. The author of Hidayah comments that Muhammad's view balances the interests of both parties, while Abu Yusuf's view is easier to implement because the value at possession is well-known. The passage follows the order: statement of Sahibayn's view, detailed explanation of Abu Hanifa's view with proof and objection, then Sahibayn's proof and the further ikhtilaf, ending with the tarjih (preference) from the author of Hidayah.

Key Terms
فلوس (fulus): Coins typically made of copper or other base metal used as currency, as opposed to gold and silver.
مثل (mithl): An identical substitute; same quantity and quality of a fungible (mithli) thing.
قیمت (qimat): Market value or price, to be paid when returning the exact thing or its mithl is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what must a debtor return if he borrowed fulus that later become demonetized?
A) The same quantity (mithl) of fulus
B) The market value of fulus on the day of possession
C) The market value of fulus on the day of demonetization
D) Any fulus equivalent to the amount lent

Key Takeaway
In a loan of fulus that becomes demonetized, Abu Hanifa requires mithl; Abu Yusuf requires value at possession; Muhammad requires value at demonetization—all valid Hanafi positions.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Sale with Fulus by Weight: Dispute Among Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad
Ruling on sale with fulus using weight expressions, with ikhtilaf among Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the validity of a sale for fulus when the price is expressed by weight, and apply the Hanafi principle of 'urf to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Custom ('urf) can make the price known even when the number of fulus is not specified.

This passage addresses a practical issue in sales: if the price is set as 'a half dirham's worth of fulus' without stating the number, is the sale valid? The Hanafi school has internal disagreement, rooted in whether fulus are considered by weight or by count, and whether custom suffices to resolve ambiguity. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school uses 'urf to determine contractual obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Is a sale for fulus valid when the price is expressed using weight terms (like nisf dirham, daniq, qirat) without specifying the number?
The price is not a specific count of fulus coins but a weight-based measure.
2
State Zufar's objection
Zufar says the sale is invalid because fulus are counted items (ma'dudat); the number must be specified, and weight terms are ambiguous.
Zufar's position prioritizes certainty over custom.
3
Explain the Hanafi response
The Hanafis (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) respond that the customary amount of fulus for such weight units is well-known among people, so specification is unnecessary.
They rely on 'urf (custom) to make the price known.
4
Note the further ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Muhammad restricts this ruling to amounts less than a dirham, because custom only covers small transactions; Abu Yusuf allows it even for a full dirham because that too is known by custom.
The dispute is about the scope of custom.
5
Identify the tarjih
The commentator states that Abu Yusuf's view is more correct (asahh), especially in the author's region. This is the mufta bihi.
The preferred position makes the sale valid in all cases where custom defines the amount.

کوئی چیز نصف درہم فلوس کے بدلے خریدی تو مشتری پر اس قدر فلوس واجب ہوں گے جن کو نصف درہم کے عوض بیچا جاتا ہے
قال ومن اشترى شيئا بنصف درهم فلوس جاز و عليه ما يباع بنصف درهم من الفلوس وكذا اذا قال بدائق فلوس وبقيراط فلوس جاز وقال زفر لا يجوز فى جميع ذلك لانه اشترى بالفلوس وانها تقدر بالعدد لا بالدائق ونصف الدرهم فلا بد من بيان عددها ونحن نقول ما يباع بالدائق ونصف الدرهم من الفلوس معلوم عند الناس والكلام فيه فاغنى عن بيان العدد ولو قال بدرهم فلوس او بدرهمين فلوس فكذلك عند ابي يوسف لان ما يباع بالدرهم من الفلوس معلوم وهو المراد لا وزن الدرهم من الفلوس وعن محمد انه لا يجوز بالدرهم ويجوز فيما دون الدرهم لان فى العادة المبايعة بالفلوس فيما دون الدرهم فصار معلوما بحكم العادة ولا كذلك الدرهم قالوا و قول ابي يوسف اصح لاسيما في ديارنا
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے کوئی چیز نصف درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدی تو جائز ہے اور مشتری پر اس قدر فلوس واجب ہوں گے جن کو نصف درہم کے عوض بیچا جاتا ہے اور اسی طرح اگر اس نے کہا بدانق فلوس یا بقیراط فلوس تو جائز ہے اور زفر نے کہا ان سب میں جائز نہیں کیونکہ اس نے فلوس کے بدلے خریدا اور فلوس کا شمار عدد سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ دانق اور نصف درہم سے پس ان کی تعداد کا بیان ضروری ہے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جو دانق اور نصف درہم کے بدلے بیچا جاتا ہے وہ لوگوں کو معلوم ہے اور اس میں گفتگو ہے پس اس نے تعداد کے بیان سے بے نیاز کر دیا اور اگر اس نے کہا بدرہم فلوس یا بدرہمین فلوس تو اسی طرح جائز ہے ابو یوسف کے نزدیک کیونکہ جو درہم کے بدلے فلوس بیچا جاتا ہے وہ معلوم ہے اور وہی مراد ہے نہ کہ درہم کے وزن کے برابر فلوس اور محمد سے مروی ہے کہ درہم کے ساتھ جائز نہیں اور درہم سے کم میں جائز ہے کیونکہ عادتاً فلوس کے ساتھ بیع درہم سے کم میں ہوتی ہے پس عادت کے حکم سے معلوم ہو گیا اور اسی طرح درہم نہیں ہے۔ کہا گیا ابو یوسف کا قول زیادہ صحیح ہے خاص کر ہمارے دیار میں۔
If someone buys something for half a dirham's worth of fulus, then the buyer will owe the amount of fulus that are sold for half a dirham.
He said: And whoever buys something for half a dirham of fulus, it is valid, and upon him is what is sold for half a dirham of fulus. Similarly, if he says: for a daniq of fulus, or for a qirat of fulus, it is valid. Zufar said: All of it is not valid, because he bought with fulus, and fulus are measured by number, not by daniq and half dirham; so stating the number is necessary. And we say: What is sold for a daniq and half dirham of fulus is known among the people, and the speech is about it, so it suffices without stating the number. And if he says: for a dirham of fulus, or for two dirhams of fulus, it is likewise valid according to Abu Yusuf, because what is sold for a dirham of fulus is known, and that is intended, not the weight of a dirham of fulus. And from Muhammad that it is not valid with dirham, and is valid for less than a dirham, because customarily buying and selling with fulus is for less than a dirham; so it becomes known by virtue of custom, and not so for dirham. They said: Abu Yusuf's saying is more correct, especially in our lands.
Translation: And if someone bought something for half a dirham of fulus, it is valid, and the buyer owes the amount of fulus that are sold for half a dirham. Similarly, if he said: for a daniq of fulus or for a qirat of fulus, it is valid. Zufar said: None of these are valid because he bought with fulus, and fulus are counted by number, not by daniq and half dirham; so stating the number is necessary. And we say: What is sold for a daniq and half dirham is known to people, and the speech is about it, so it suffices without stating the number. And if he said: for a dirham of fulus or for two dirhams of fulus, it is likewise valid according to Abu Yusuf, because what is sold for a dirham of fulus is known, and that is intended, not the weight of a dirham of fulus. And from Muhammad that it is not valid with dirham, and is valid for less than a dirham, because customarily buying and selling with fulus is for less than a dirham; so it becomes known by virtue of custom, and not so for dirham. It was said: Abu Yusuf's saying is more correct, especially in our lands.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of a sale when the price is expressed in fulus using weight-based terms like 'half dirham' or 'daniq'. The passage begins with a ruling: if a person buys something for half a dirham's worth of fulus, the buyer must give the amount of fulus that are customarily sold for half a dirham (not a specific number). The same applies if the price is stated in daniq or qirat. Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, objects that fulus are counted (ma'dudat) and thus the number must be specified; weight-based terms are ambiguous. The Hanafi response is that such amounts are well-known by custom ('urf), so specification is unnecessary. The passage then addresses the case when the price is a full dirham or two dirhams of fulus: according to Abu Yusuf, it is valid because the customary amount for a dirham is known; but according to Imam Muhammad, it is only valid if the price is less than a dirham, because custom only recognizes fulus transactions for amounts less than a dirham. The commentator (of Hidayah) states that Abu Yusuf's view is more correct (asahh), especially in the author's region. The passage follows the order: statement of the ruling, Zufar's objection, the Hanafi refutation, then the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and finally the tarjih (preference) for Abu Yusuf's view.

Key Terms
دانق (daniq): A unit of weight: 1/6 of a dirham, used as a measure for fulus.
قیراط (qirat): A small weight unit, often 1/20 of a dirham, used in trade.
عرف (urf): Customary practice of the people regarding transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is invalid because fulus must be counted
B) The sale is valid only if less than a dirham
C) The sale is valid, and the buyer pays the customary amount for a dirham of fulus
D) The sale is valid only if the buyer and seller agree on a number later

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, customary practice ('urf) can remove ambiguity in the price of fulus, making sales valid even without specifying the number of coins, as affirmed by the tarjih favoring Abu Yusuf's view.

Valuation of Fulus Upon Cessation: Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation of obsolete currency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the valuation date of fulus when they become obsolete and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When fulus become obsolete, valuation date is disputed: possession day (Abu Yusuf) vs cessation day (Muhammad).

This passage from al-Hidayah examines a practical problem: a loan of fulus (copper coins) that later go out of circulation. While all Hanafi imams agree the debtor must pay the value, they differ on which date's value to use. The dispute reflects a tension between ease of implementation and balancing the interests of both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify common ground among the three imams
All agree that when fulus become obsolete, the debtor must compensate. But they differ on the basis: Abu Hanifa says the like (mithl) is due; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say value (qimah) is due, differing on the date.
Abu Hanifa's view is the outlier: he requires mithl even if impossible, while his students accept qimah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the debtor must return the like (mithl) of fulus, not the value. However, the passage implies this is impractical when fulus are obsolete, leading to his students' alternative.
The text contrasts Abu Hanifa's view with that of his students.
3
Contrast Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's positions
Abu Yusuf: value at the day the debtor took possession (yawm al-qabd). Muhammad: value at the day the fulus ceased circulation (yawm al-inqita').
Both accept qimah but differ on the temporal reference point.
4
Examine the reasoning of each
Abu Yusuf prioritizes ease and certainty: the possession date is known to all. Muhammad prioritizes fairness: his date balances the interests of both lender and borrower.
Al-Marghinani explains that Muhammad's view gives consideration to both parties.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of al-Hidayah notes that Abu Yusuf's view is easier to implement and is preferred in practice, though Muhammad's view is more balanced. Thus, the operative ruling for fatwa is Abu Yusuf's position.
The text says 'asahh' (more correct) in their land, indicating reliance.

It is not possible in their meaning in which the attribute of being a price exists. So when current fulus which the debtor had taken, returning their like became impossible, then returning their value becomes obligatory. Just as if a person took wheat or other fungible thing as a loan and then it disappeared from the market, then returning its value becomes obligatory. Similarly in the mentioned issue, returning the value will be obligatory. However, there is this much: according to Qadi Abu Yusuf, the value of the day the debtor took possession is obligatory. And according to Imam Muhammad, the value of the day their circulation ceased is obligatory. This difference has already passed. The origin of the difference between the two is in this issue: if a person usurped a fungible thing and then it became unavailable, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the value on the day of usurpation is obligatory, and according to Imam Muhammad, the value on the day of unavailability is obligatory. The author of Hidayah says: In Imam Muhammad's view, consideration is given to both the lender and the borrower. Consideration for the lender is in contrast to Imam Abu Hanifa's view because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the like of these fulus is obligatory, and obviously there is no consideration for the lender because he is giving current fulus and receiving the like of fulus. And in contrast to Imam Abu Yusuf's view, there is consideration for the borrower in this way: according to Abu Yusuf, the value on the day of possession is obligatory, and since on the day the borrower took possession, the fulus were current, their value would be higher, and there is no consideration for the borrower. So it became apparent that in Imam Muhammad's view, consideration for both debtor and creditor is kept in mind. And in Imam Abu Yusuf's view, there is more ease because the value on the day the borrower took possession is known to the creditor, debtor, and all people. Therefore, acting upon it is easy. And the value on the day of unavailability is ambiguous for people and there will be severe disagreement in it. Therefore, determining the value on the day of unavailability and applying the legal ruling is not easy.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the valuation date for returning fulus (copper coins) when they have become obsolete. The ruling is that when fulus are given as a loan and then go out of circulation, the debtor must pay their value rather than the like. The dispute centers on which date's value should be used. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the value is determined as of the day the debtor took possession (yawm al-qabd), while Imam Muhammad holds it is the day the fulus ceased to circulate (yawm al-inqita'). The author of the Hidayah (al-Marghinani) provides a rationale: Muhammad's view balances the interests of both parties, giving the creditor fair compensation and the debtor a manageable burden, whereas Abu Yusuf's view is easier to implement because the value at the time of possession is widely known. The text does not cite explicit Quranic or hadith proofs but relies on juristic reasoning (istihsan and consideration of ease).

Key Terms
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as currency, distinct from silver dirhams and gold dinars.
مثل (mithl): An equivalent in kind and quantity, applicable to fungible goods (mithliyyat).
انقطاع (inqita'): The cessation of circulation or availability of a currency or fungible good in the market.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The day of judgment

Key Takeaway
When fulus become obsolete, the debtor must pay value; the Hanafi school's mufta bihi is the value at possession, though Muhammad's cessation view is more balanced.

Buying with Fulus Expressed in Dirham Fractions: Validity and the Role of Custom
Ruling on sale when price is fulus specified by weight fractions, with disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a sale where the price is fulus specified by dirham fractions, distinguish the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and evaluate Zufar's objection.

Core Idea
When custom defines the quantity, uncertainty dissolves — the sale is valid.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani presents a nuanced ruling on a common transaction: buying goods with copper coins (fulus) while specifying the price as a fraction of a silver dirham. The key question is whether such a vague price specification renders the sale invalid due to ignorance (jahalah). The Hanafi school, relying on custom ('urf), defends its validity against the objection of Imam Zufar. We will unpack the dispute and the intra-Hanafi divergence between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
1. State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
Read the opening sentence: 'Whoever buys something with half a dirham of fulus, it is valid.' The ruling extends to daniq and qirat. The basis is that people customarily know how many fulus correspond to those fractional weights, so the price is known.
The Hanafi principle: 'What is known by custom is like a stated condition.'
2
2. Identify Zufar's objection and the Hanafi response
Zufar argues that fulus are counted by number, not weighed, so specifying by weight does not determine quantity, causing gharar (uncertainty). The Hanafi response: custom has made the correspondence well-known, so no jahalah remains. The intention is to buy fulus equivalent to that weight.
The dispute is about the method of estimation: counting vs. inferred by custom.
3
3. Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement (Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad)
Abu Yusuf extends the ruling to a full dirham or more, because the customary equivalent is still known. Muhammad restricts it to amounts less than a dirham, as transactions with fulus for larger sums were uncommon in his era. Note the author's preference: 'Qawl Abi Yusuf asahh' (Abu Yusuf's view is more correct), especially in the author's region.
This shows how custom can change over time and place.
4
4. Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical effect: in a sale where the price is 'two dirhams of fulus' without specifying the number, Abu Yusuf would validate it, Muhammad would invalidate it, and Zufar would invalidate any such transaction. The mufta bihi (operative view) is Abu Yusuf's, especially where such transactions are customary.
The mufti must consider local custom when applying this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اشترى شيئا بنصف درهم فلوس جاز وعليه ما يباع بنصف درهم من الفلوس وكذا اذا قال بدائق فلوس وبقيراط فلوس جاز وقال زفر لا يجوز فى جميع ذلك لانه اشترى بالفلوس وانها تقدر بالعدد لا بالدائق ونصف الدرهم فلا بد من بيان عددها ونحن نقول ما يباع بالدائق ونصف الدرهم من الفلوس معلوم عند الناس والكلام فيه فاغنى عن بيان العدد ولو قال بدرهم فلوس او بدرهمين فلوس فكذلك عند ابي يوسف لان ما يباع بالدرهم من الفلوس معلوم وهو المراد لا وزن الدرهم من الفلوس وعن محمد انه لا يجوز بالدرهم ويجوز فيما دون الدرهم لان فى العادة المبايعة بالفلوس فيما دون الدرهم فصار معلوما بحكم العادة ولا كذلك الدرهم قالوا وقول ابي يوسف اصح لاسيما في ديارنا
He said: Whoever buys something with half a dirham of fulus, it is valid, and upon him is what is sold for half a dirham of fulus. Similarly, if he says with a daniq of fulus or with a qirat of fulus, it is valid. Zufar said: All of that is not valid because he bought with fulus, and they are estimated by number, not by daniq and half dirham, so their number must be stated. We say: what is sold for a daniq and half dirham of fulus is known among people, and the talk is about that, so it dispenses with stating the number. And if he says with a dirham of fulus or with two dirhams of fulus, then it is similar according to Abu Yusuf, because what is sold for a dirham of fulus is known, and that is what is intended, not the weight of a dirham of fulus. And it is narrated from Muhammad that it is not valid with a dirham, but it is valid with less than a dirham, because customarily transactions with fulus are for less than a dirham, so it becomes known by custom, unlike a dirham. They said: The statement of Abu Yusuf is more correct, especially in our lands.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a sale where the price (thaman) is fulus (copper coins) but the contract specifies the price in terms of fractions of a silver dirham (e.g., half dirham, daniq, qirat). The ruling is that such a sale is valid according to the majority of Hanafis (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad as reported), because the quantity of fulus that corresponds to that weight is customarily known. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi dissenter) argues that fulus are counted, not weighed, so the number must be specified. The Hanafi response is that custom ('urf) makes the quantity known, so specifying the number is unnecessary. The dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad concerns whether this applies to a full dirham or more. Abu Yusuf extends the ruling to dirhams, while Muhammad restricts it to amounts less than a dirham, citing that transactions with fulus are customarily for smaller amounts. The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) prefers Abu Yusuf's view, especially in their own land.

Key Terms
دائق (daniq): A unit of weight equal to one-sixth of a dirham.
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight equal to one-twelfth of a dirham (half a daniq).
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used as money; here they are the medium of exchange but the contract specifies their value in silver fractions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Buying with Fulus for Fractional Dirhams: The Role of Custom
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fulus sale for fractional dirhams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on buying with fulus for half a dirham, daniq, or qirat, and explain how custom (urf) makes the price known.

Core Idea
When custom fixes the number of fulus for a given silver value, the price is known and the sale is valid.

This lesson examines a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the sale of an item in exchange for fulus (copper coins) when the price is expressed as a fraction of a dirham (half dirham, daniq, qirat). The central question is whether the price is known enough for the contract to be valid. We will explore Imam Zufar's objection and the majority response that relies on custom (urf) to supply the missing information.

Guided Path
1
State the Majority Position
Identify the ruling that buying an item for half a dirham, a daniq, or a qirat of fulus is valid. Note that the fulus in question are those whose silver value is well-known by common practice.
The majority includes Imams Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on this point.
2
Analyze Imam Zufar's Objection
Understand Zufar's reasoning: fulus are counted items (maddudat), so the number must be explicitly mentioned. Specifying a weight (e.g., half dirham) does not indicate count, making the price unknown and the sale invalid.
Zufar's position is that the contract fails due to gharar (uncertainty) in the price.
3
Examine the Hanafi Response Using Custom
See how the majority counters: when it is common knowledge how many fulus are given for a given silver value, the number is effectively known. Custom (urf) supplies the missing detail, so the price is not unknown.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that 'al-ma'ruf 'urfan ka al-mashrut shartan' (what is known by custom is like a stipulated condition).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصرف
اشرف البدایہ جلد ضمیم
درہم کے عوض بیچا جاتا ہے اور اسی طرح اگر کہا کہ ایک دائق فلوس کے عوض یا ایک قیراط فلوس کے عوض خریدی تو جائز ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ ان تمام صورتوں میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے فلوس کے عوض خریدا ہے اور فلوس کا اندازہ عدد سے کیا جاتا ہے نہ کہ دائق اور نصف درہم سے لہذا فلوس کے عدد کا بیان کرنا ضروری ہے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وہ فلوس جن کو دائق اور نصف درہم سے فروخت کیا جاتا ہے لوگوں کے نزدیک معلوم ہیں۔ اور کلام اس میں ہے۔ اس عدد کے بیان کرنے سے بے نیاز ہو گیا ہے اور اگر کہا ایک درہم فلوس کے عوض یا دو درہم فلوس کے عوض تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایسا ہی ہے اسلئے کہ وہ فلوس جن کو درہم کے عوض بیچا جاتا ہے معلوم ہیں۔ اور یہی مراد ہے نہ کہ فلوس میں سے درہم کا وزن اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ درہم میں جائز نہیں اور درہم سے کم میں جائز ہے کیونکہ درہم سے کم میں فلوس کے عوض خرید و فروخت کرنے کی عادت ہے۔ پس عادت کی وجہ سے (نصف درہم کے پیسے ) معلوم ہو گئے اور در ہم ایسا نہیں ہے۔ مشائخ نے کہا کہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول اصح ہے خصوصاً ہمارے ملک میں۔
تشریح وافق جمع دوائق اور دوانیق آتی ہے ایک دائق درہم کا چھٹا حصہ ہوتا ہے۔ قیراط جمع قراریط آتی ہے۔ قیراط دائق کا نصف ہوتا ہے یعنی ایک درہم کا بارہواں حصہ قیراط کہلاتا ہے درہم چاندی کا ہوتا ہے اور فلوس چاندی کے علاوہ تانبے وغیرہ کے ہوتے ہیں۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کہا کہ میں نے یہ چیز نصف درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدی یعنی اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریدی جن کی قیمت نصف درہم چاندی ہو تو یہ بیع جائز ہے اور مشتری پر اتنے فلوس کا ادا کرنا واجب ہو گا جو نصف درہم کے عوض کہتے ہیں اور اگر یہ کہا کہ یہ چیز میں نے ایک دائق فلوس یا ایک قیراط فلوس کے عوض خریدی یعنی اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریدی جن کی قیمت ایک دائق چاندی یا ایک قیراط چاندی ہو تو یہ بھی جائز ہے اور مشتری پر اتنے فلوس کا ادا کرنا واجب ہے جو ایک دائق چاندی یا ایک قیراط چاندی کے عوض بکتے ہوں اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ ان تمام صورتوں میں بیع نا جائز ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری نے فلوس کے عوض خریداری کی ہے اور فلوس معدودات میں سے ہیں اور نصف درہم، دانق اور قیراط موزونات میں سے ہیں۔ یعنی فلوس کا اندازہ گن کر کیا جاتا ہے۔ دائق قیراط اور نصف درہم سے نہیں کیا جاتا۔ پس نصف درہم اور دائق اور قیراط کے ذکر سے فلوس کے عدد کا ذکر نہیں ہوا۔ اور جب فلوس کے عدد کا ذکر اور بیان نہیں ہوا تو اس بیع میں فلوس کی مقدار یعنی ثمن مجہول رہا اور ثمن مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں بیع نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے ان تمام صورتوں میں بیع نا جائز ہو گی۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ جو فلوس، نصف درہم اور دانق اور قیراط کے عوض بکتے ہیں وہ سب ہی کو معلوم ہیں۔ اور ہم نے مسئلہ بھی اسی صورت میں فرض کیا ہے جبکہ لوگوں کو یہ معلوم ہو کہ نصف درہم چاندی کے عوض کس قدر فلوس بکتے ہیں اور ایک دانق کے عوض کس قدر اور ایک قیراط کے عوض کس قدر فلوس بکتے ہیں اور مسئلہ بھی اسی صورت میں فرض کیا گیا ہے تو فلوس کی مقدار اور تعداد بیان کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب اس کا علم سب ہی کو ہے تو ثمن کا مجہول ہونا لازم نہ آئے گا۔ اور جب ثمن مجہول نہ رہا تو بیع بھی نا جائز نہ ہوگی بلکہ جائز ہو گی۔ اور اگر یہ کہا کہ میں نے یہ چیز ایک درہم فلوس یا دو درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدی یعنی اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریدی جن کی قیمت ایک درہم یا دو درہم چاندی ہو تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس طرح کی بیع ایک درہم میں تو جائز نہیں ہے مگر ایک درہم سے کم میں جائز ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ فلوس جو ایک درہم کے عوض بکتے ہیں لوگوں کو ان کی مقدار اور عدد معلوم ہے اور یہاں یہی مراد ہے کہ اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریداری کی جن کی قیمت ایک درہم چاندی ہو۔ یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریدے جن کا وزن ایک درہم کے وزن کے برابر ہو۔ پس جب یہ معلوم ہے کہ کس قدر فلوس ایک درہم چاندی کے عوض بکتے ہیں تو اس صورت میں بھی عقد بیع کا ثمن مجہول نہ رہا اور جب ثمن مجہول نہیں ہے تو بیع بھی جائز اور درست ہوگی۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک درہم سے کم میں تو فلوس سے خریدنے کی لوگوں میں عادت ہے لیکن ایک درہم میں فلوس سے خریدنے کی لوگوں میں عادت نہیں ہے۔ پس چونکہ عادت کی وجہ سے نصف درہم کے پیسے تو معلوم ہو جائیں گے لیکن درہم کے فلوس اور پیسے معلوم نہ ہوں گے۔ اس لئے نصف درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدنا تو جائز ہو گا مگر ایک درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدنا جائز نہ ہو گا۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ خصوصا ماوراء النہر کے شہروں میں اسلئے کہ یہاں کے لوگ درہم کے عوض بھی فلوس خریدتے ہیں۔ پس ایک درہم چاندی کے عوض جس قدر فلوس بکتے ہیں یہاں کے لوگوں کو چونکہ ان کی مقدار معلوم ہے اسلئے ایک درہم فلوس یا دو درہم فلوس کے عوض خریداری کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔
Book of Sarf (Money Exchange). Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume supplement. If one buys an item in exchange for fulus (copper coins) to the value of half a dirham, it is valid. Similarly, if he says, 'I bought in exchange for a daniq of fulus' or 'a qirat of fulus', it is valid. Imam Zufar said: In all these cases it is not valid. Because he bought in exchange for fulus, and fulus are measured by count, not by daniq or half dirham. Therefore, it is necessary to mention the number of fulus. We say: Those fulus which are sold in exchange for a daniq or half dirham are well-known among people. The speech is about that. The mention of the number has been dispensed with. And if he said, 'one dirham of fulus' or 'two dirhams of fulus', then according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is the same, because those fulus which are sold in exchange for a dirham are known. That is the intended meaning, not the weight of the dirham in fulus. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that it is not valid for a dirham, but valid for less than a dirham, because the custom of buying and selling fulus for less than a dirham exists. Due to custom, the fulus for half a dirham become known, not for a dirham. The mashayikh said: The saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is more correct, especially in our country. Explanation: wafq (?) plural of daniq is dawaniq. A daniq is one-sixth of a dirham. Qirat plural is qararit. A qirat is half a daniq, i.e., one-twelfth of a dirham. A dirham is of silver, and fulus are of copper etc. The scenario is: a person said, 'I bought this item in exchange for half a dirham of fulus', i.e., in exchange for fulus whose value is half a dirham of silver; this sale is valid, and the buyer must pay the fulus that are given for half a dirham. If he said, 'I bought in exchange for a daniq of fulus' or 'a qirat of fulus', i.e., in exchange for fulus whose value is a daniq or qirat of silver, this is also valid, and the buyer must pay the fulus that are sold for a daniq or qirat of silver. Imam Zufar said: In all these cases the sale is invalid. Imam Zufar's proof is: The buyer purchased in exchange for fulus, and fulus are counted items, while half dirham, daniq, and qirat are weighed items. Fulus are valued by count, not by daniq, qirat, or half dirham. So mentioning half dirham, daniq, or qirat does not mention the number of fulus. When the number of fulus is not mentioned, the price (thaman) in the sale is unknown, and when the price is unknown, the sale is invalid. Therefore, in all these cases the sale is invalid. Our response: The fulus that are sold for half a dirham, daniq, and qirat are known to everyone. We have assumed the case only when people know how many fulus are sold for half a dirham of silver, how many for a daniq, and how many for a qirat. And the case is assumed in this condition, so there is no need to mention the quantity and number of fulus. When everyone knows it, the price is not unknown. When the price is not unknown, the sale will not be invalid, but valid. And if he said, 'I bought this item in exchange for one dirham of fulus' or 'two dirhams of fulus', i.e., in exchange for fulus whose value is one dirham or two dirhams of silver, then it is valid according to Imam Abu Yusuf, and according to Imam Muhammad, such a sale is not valid for one dirham but valid for less than one dirham. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof: Those fulus that are sold for one dirham are known to people in quantity and number, and here the intention is that he bought in exchange for fulus whose value is one dirham of silver. It is not intended that he bought fulus whose weight equals the weight of a dirham. So when it is known how many fulus are sold for one dirham of silver, then in this case the price is not unknown, and when the price is not unknown, the sale is valid and correct. Imam Muhammad's proof: For less than one dirham, people have the custom of buying with fulus, but for one dirham, people do not have the custom of buying with fulus. So due to custom, the fulus for half a dirham become known, but the fulus for a dirham are not known. Therefore, buying in exchange for half a dirham of fulus is valid, but buying in exchange for one dirham of fulus is not valid. The mashayikh said: The saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is more correct, especially in the cities of Transoxiana, because the people there also buy fulus for dirhams. So since they know the quantity of fulus sold for one dirham of silver, buying in exchange for one dirham of fulus or two dirhams of fulus is also valid.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of buying with fulus (copper coins) where the price is specified as a fraction of a dirham (half dirham, daniq, qirat) or a full dirham. The core issue is whether the price is known (ma'lum) when the count of fulus is not explicitly given but the value in silver is mentioned. Imam Zufar argues that fulus are counted items, so their number must be known; specifying weight (half dirham, etc.) does not indicate count, making the price unknown and the sale invalid. The majority (Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, and the commentator) respond that custom (urf) makes the quantity known: if people commonly sell fulus for a given silver value, the number is effectively known, and the price is not unknown. On the question of buying for a full dirham, Imam Abu Yusuf permits it because the custom is established (especially in Transoxiana), while Imam Muhammad restricts validity to less than a dirham due to lack of custom at that amount. The mashayikh prefer Abu Yusuf's view. The passage demonstrates how Hanafi fiqh uses custom (urf) to determine knowledge in contracts, and shows the hierarchy of opinions: Zufar's view is overruled, and between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, Abu Yusuf's is deemed more correct, especially for certain regions.

Key Terms
درہم (dirham): A silver coin, standard unit of currency in Islamic law; used as a measure of value.
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins, considered as counted (maddudat) items in sales.
دائق (daniq): One-sixth of a dirham; a unit of weight/value.
قیراط (qirat): Half a daniq, one-twelfth of a dirham.
عادت (adah (custom)): The prevailing practice among people; used to determine knowledge of the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority view, why is buying an item for 'a daniq of fulus' valid without mentioning the count?
A) Because daniq is a unit of weight, and fulus are sold by weight.
B) Because the custom of the area determines the number of fulus for a daniq, making it known.
C) Because the buyer and seller can always agree later on the number.
D) Because the sale is considered a barter transaction.

Key Takeaway
When custom makes the quantity of fulus for a given silver value widely known, the price is considered known and the sale is valid.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
The Full Dirham Dispute: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad and the Tarjih
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the full dirham case with tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding buying with fulus for a full dirham, and state the mufta bihi position preferred by later scholars.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Yusuf validates the sale for a full dirham based on custom; Imam Muhammad restricts to less than a dirham; the mashayikh prefer Abu Yusuf.

This lesson deepens the discussion to the case where the price is expressed as a full dirham of fulus. While both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree on fractions, they differ on a whole dirham. We will examine their proofs and see how the later mashayikh (scholars) made a tarjih, preferring Abu Yusuf's view, especially in regions like Transoxiana where the custom was strong.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disagreement
Note that the dispute is between Imam Abu Yusuf (sale valid for a full dirham) and Imam Muhammad (only valid for less than a dirham). Both agree on fractions.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
State Abu Yusuf's Proof
Abu Yusuf argues that if the customary exchange rate for a dirham of fulus is known, the price is known. The intention is the silver value, not weight, so custom supplies the count.
His proof relies on the same custom argument used for fractions.
3
State Muhammad's Proof
Muhammad argues that the custom of buying with fulus for a full dirham is not widespread; people only customarily use fulus for small amounts (less than a dirham). Therefore, the number is not known for a full dirham, making the price unknown.
Muhammad distinguishes based on the prevalence of custom.
4
Explain the Tarjih and Its Basis
The mashayikh (later scholars) prefer Abu Yusuf's view, especially in areas where the custom of using fulus for full dirhams is established (e.g., Transoxiana). The basis is that custom is a valid determiner of knowledge, and once established, it applies equally to all amounts.
This shows that the application of custom can be regional; different locales may have different customs.

مشتری پر اتنے فلوس کا ادا کرنا واجب ہو گا جو نصف درہم کے عوض کہتے ہیں اور اگر یہ کہا کہ یہ چیز میں نے ایک دائق فلوس یا ایک قیراط فلوس کے عوض خریدی یعنی اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریدی جن کی قیمت ایک دائق چاندی یا ایک قیراط چاندی ہو تو یہ بھی جائز ہے اور مشتری پر اتنے فلوس کا ادا کرنا واجب ہے جو ایک دائق چاندی یا ایک قیراط چاندی کے عوض بکتے ہوں اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ ان تمام صورتوں میں بیع نا جائز ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری نے فلوس کے عوض خریداری کی ہے اور فلوس معدودات میں سے ہیں اور نصف درہم، دانق اور قیراط موزونات میں سے ہیں۔ یعنی فلوس کا اندازہ گن کر کیا جاتا ہے۔ دائق قیراط اور نصف درہم سے نہیں کیا جاتا۔ پس نصف درہم اور دائق اور قیراط کے ذکر سے فلوس کے عدد کا ذکر نہیں ہوا۔ اور جب فلوس کے عدد کا ذکر اور بیان نہیں ہوا تو اس بیع میں فلوس کی مقدار یعنی ثمن مجہول رہا اور ثمن مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں بیع نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے ان تمام صورتوں میں بیع نا جائز ہو گی۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ جو فلوس، نصف درہم اور دانق اور قیراط کے عوض بکتے ہیں وہ سب ہی کو معلوم ہیں۔ اور ہم نے مسئلہ بھی اسی صورت میں فرض کیا ہے جبکہ لوگوں کو یہ معلوم ہو کہ نصف درہم چاندی کے عوض کس قدر فلوس بکتے ہیں اور ایک دانق کے عوض کس قدر اور ایک قیراط کے عوض کس قدر فلوس بکتے ہیں اور مسئلہ بھی اسی صورت میں فرض کیا گیا ہے تو فلوس کی مقدار اور تعداد بیان کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب اس کا علم سب ہی کو ہے تو ثمن کا مجہول ہونا لازم نہ آئے گا۔ اور جب ثمن مجہول نہ رہا تو بیع بھی نا جائز نہ ہوگی بلکہ جائز ہو گی۔ اور اگر یہ کہا کہ میں نے یہ چیز ایک درہم فلوس یا دو درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدی یعنی اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریدی جن کی قیمت ایک درہم یا دو درہم چاندی ہو تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس طرح کی بیع ایک درہم میں تو جائز نہیں ہے مگر ایک درہم سے کم میں جائز ہے۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ فلوس جو ایک درہم کے عوض بکتے ہیں لوگوں کو ان کی مقدار اور عدد معلوم ہے اور یہاں یہی مراد ہے کہ اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریداری کی جن کی قیمت ایک درہم چاندی ہو۔ یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ اتنے فلوس کے عوض خریدے جن کا وزن ایک درہم کے وزن کے برابر ہو۔ پس جب یہ معلوم ہے کہ کس قدر فلوس ایک درہم چاندی کے عوض بکتے ہیں تو اس صورت میں بھی عقد بیع کا ثمن مجہول نہ رہا اور جب ثمن مجہول نہیں ہے تو بیع بھی جائز اور درست ہوگی۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک درہم سے کم میں تو فلوس سے خریدنے کی لوگوں میں عادت ہے لیکن ایک درہم میں فلوس سے خریدنے کی لوگوں میں عادت نہیں ہے۔ پس چونکہ عادت کی وجہ سے نصف درہم کے پیسے تو معلوم ہو جائیں گے لیکن درہم کے فلوس اور پیسے معلوم نہ ہوں گے۔ اس لئے نصف درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدنا تو جائز ہو گا مگر ایک درہم فلوس کے عوض خریدنا جائز نہ ہو گا۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ خصوصا ماوراء النہر کے شہروں میں اسلئے کہ یہاں کے لوگ درہم کے عوض بھی فلوس خریدتے ہیں۔ پس ایک درہم چاندی کے عوض جس قدر فلوس بکتے ہیں یہاں کے لوگوں کو چونکہ ان کی مقدار معلوم ہے اسلئے ایک درہم فلوس یا دو درہم فلوس کے عوض خریداری کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔
Book of Sarf (Money Exchange). Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume supplement. If one buys an item in exchange for fulus (copper coins) to the value of half a dirham, it is valid. Similarly, if he says, 'I bought in exchange for a daniq of fulus' or 'a qirat of fulus', it is valid. Imam Zufar said: In all these cases it is not valid. Because he bought in exchange for fulus, and fulus are measured by count, not by daniq or half dirham. Therefore, it is necessary to mention the number of fulus. We say: Those fulus which are sold in exchange for a daniq or half dirham are well-known among people. The speech is about that. The mention of the number has been dispensed with. And if he said, 'one dirham of fulus' or 'two dirhams of fulus', then according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is the same, because those fulus which are sold in exchange for a dirham are known. That is the intended meaning, not the weight of the dirham in fulus. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that it is not valid for a dirham, but valid for less than a dirham, because the custom of buying and selling fulus for less than a dirham exists. Due to custom, the fulus for half a dirham become known, not for a dirham. The mashayikh said: The saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is more correct, especially in our country. Explanation: wafq (?) plural of daniq is dawaniq. A daniq is one-sixth of a dirham. Qirat plural is qararit. A qirat is half a daniq, i.e., one-twelfth of a dirham. A dirham is of silver, and fulus are of copper etc. The scenario is: a person said, 'I bought this item in exchange for half a dirham of fulus', i.e., in exchange for fulus whose value is half a dirham of silver; this sale is valid, and the buyer must pay the fulus that are given for half a dirham. If he said, 'I bought in exchange for a daniq of fulus' or 'a qirat of fulus', i.e., in exchange for fulus whose value is a daniq or qirat of silver, this is also valid, and the buyer must pay the fulus that are sold for a daniq or qirat of silver. Imam Zufar said: In all these cases the sale is invalid. Imam Zufar's proof is: The buyer purchased in exchange for fulus, and fulus are counted items, while half dirham, daniq, and qirat are weighed items. Fulus are valued by count, not by daniq, qirat, or half dirham. So mentioning half dirham, daniq, or qirat does not mention the number of fulus. When the number of fulus is not mentioned, the price (thaman) in the sale is unknown, and when the price is unknown, the sale is invalid. Therefore, in all these cases the sale is invalid. Our response: The fulus that are sold for half a dirham, daniq, and qirat are known to everyone. We have assumed the case only when people know how many fulus are sold for half a dirham of silver, how many for a daniq, and how many for a qirat. And the case is assumed in this condition, so there is no need to mention the quantity and number of fulus. When everyone knows it, the price is not unknown. When the price is not unknown, the sale will not be invalid, but valid. And if he said, 'I bought this item in exchange for one dirham of fulus' or 'two dirhams of fulus', i.e., in exchange for fulus whose value is one dirham or two dirhams of silver, then it is valid according to Imam Abu Yusuf, and according to Imam Muhammad, such a sale is not valid for one dirham but valid for less than one dirham. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof: Those fulus that are sold for one dirham are known to people in quantity and number, and here the intention is that he bought in exchange for fulus whose value is one dirham of silver. It is not intended that he bought fulus whose weight equals the weight of a dirham. So when it is known how many fulus are sold for one dirham of silver, then in this case the price is not unknown, and when the price is not unknown, the sale is valid and correct. Imam Muhammad's proof: For less than one dirham, people have the custom of buying with fulus, but for one dirham, people do not have the custom of buying with fulus. So due to custom, the fulus for half a dirham become known, but the fulus for a dirham are not known. Therefore, buying in exchange for half a dirham of fulus is valid, but buying in exchange for one dirham of fulus is not valid. The mashayikh said: The saying of Imam Abu Yusuf is more correct, especially in the cities of Transoxiana, because the people there also buy fulus for dirhams. So since they know the quantity of fulus sold for one dirham of silver, buying in exchange for one dirham of fulus or two dirhams of fulus is also valid.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of buying with fulus (copper coins) where the price is specified as a fraction of a dirham (half dirham, daniq, qirat) or a full dirham. The core issue is whether the price is known (ma'lum) when the count of fulus is not explicitly given but the value in silver is mentioned. Imam Zufar argues that fulus are counted items, so their number must be known; specifying weight (half dirham, etc.) does not indicate count, making the price unknown and the sale invalid. The majority (Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, and the commentator) respond that custom (urf) makes the quantity known: if people commonly sell fulus for a given silver value, the number is effectively known, and the price is not unknown. On the question of buying for a full dirham, Imam Abu Yusuf permits it because the custom is established (especially in Transoxiana), while Imam Muhammad restricts validity to less than a dirham due to lack of custom at that amount. The mashayikh prefer Abu Yusuf's view. The passage demonstrates how Hanafi fiqh uses custom (urf) to determine knowledge in contracts, and shows the hierarchy of opinions: Zufar's view is overruled, and between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, Abu Yusuf's is deemed more correct, especially for certain regions.

Key Terms
درہم (dirham): A silver coin used as a monetary unit.
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins, counted items.
عادت (adah (custom)): The prevailing practice; here, the custom of using fulus for transactions of a certain amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the mashayikh prefer Imam Abu Yusuf's view on buying with fulus for a full dirham?
A) Because Imam Abu Yusuf was the senior student of Abu Hanifa.
B) Because in many regions, the custom of using fulus for a dirham exists, making the price known.
C) Because Imam Muhammad's view contradicts Ijma.
D) Because the sale is always valid regardless of custom.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position, following the mashayikh, is that buying with fulus for a full dirham is valid if the customary exchange rate is known, especially in regions where such custom exists.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Split Contract with Riba: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on composite sarf transaction with riba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa voids the entire transaction while the Sahibayn split it, and apply the rule of unitary contract (safqah muttahidah) to determine validity of composite transactions.

Core Idea
In a single contract mixing valid sale and riba, Abu Hanifa voids all; the Sahibayn sever the valid part; repetition splits the contract.

This passage presents a critical intra-Hanafi disagreement on the effect of riba within a unitary transaction. The case involves giving a dirham to a money-changer and requesting both fulus (legal tender coins) and an exchange of silver that includes a slight deficiency (half dirham minus a grain). The Sahibayn treat riba as confined to its defective part, while Abu Hanifa sees strong corruption spreading to the entire contract. Understanding their reasoning clarifies the Hanafi principle of safqah muttahidah (unitary transaction) and offers a practical hila (legal stratagem) through repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction components
Recognize that the single dirham is used to purchase two things: fulus (worth half a dirham) and half a dirham minus one grain (silver). The silver exchange involves a deficiency, triggering riba al-fadl.
The first part (fulus) is a valid sarf exchange; the second part is riba because of unequal weight.
2
Note the riba element
Half a dirham minus a grain exchanged for half a dirham (the other half of the original dirham) is riba because it is a sale of silver for silver with a deficiency.
Even one grain difference in weight constitutes riba al-fadl in Hanafi fiqh.
3
State Sahibayn's view and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the sale of fulus is valid and the silver exchange is void. They treat the contract as composite: each part stands separately unless the corruption is strong in a way that spreads.
Their reasoning: the valid part is not contaminated by the invalid part because each is a separate exchange.
4
State Abu Hanifa's view and reasoning
Abu Hanifa says the entire transaction is void because it is a single contract (safqah muttahidah) and the corruption of riba is strong (qawiy), so it spreads to the whole.
The principle: when a single contract contains a forbidden element that is inherently evil (like riba), the taint covers the entire bargain.
5
Examine the hila of repeating the offer
If the person repeats the word 'a'ta' (give) twice, making two separate requests, then Abu Hanifa agrees with the Sahibayn that only the riba part is void. This is because two separate utterances create two independent contracts.
This hila resolves the dispute and is considered correct (huwa al-sahih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صراف کو ایک درہم دیا اور کہا کہ اسکے نصف کے بدلے فلوس اور دوسرے نصف کے بدلے نصف درہم ایک تہ کم دید فلوس میں بیع جائز اور بقیہ میں باطل ہے
قال ومن أعطى صيرفيا درهما وقال اعطنى بنصفه فلوسا وبنصفه نصفا الاحبة جاز البيع في الفلوس وبطل فيما بقى عندها لان بيع نصف درهم بالفلوس جائز وبيع النصف بنصف الاحبة ربو فلا يجوز، وعلى قياس قول ابي حنيفة بطل فى الكل لان الصفقة متحدة والفساد قوى فيشيع وقد مرنظيره ولو كرر لفظ الاعطاء كان جوابه كجوابهما هو الصحيح لانهما بيعان ولو قال اعطنى نصف درهم فلوسا ونصفا الاحبة جازلا نه قابل الدرهم بما يباع من الفلوس بنصف درهم و بنصف درهم الاحبة فيكون نصف درهم الاحبة بمثله وما وراء بازاء الفلوس قال رضى الله عنه وفى اكثر نسخ المختصر ذكر المسألة الثانية
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے صراف کو ایک درہم دے کر کہا کہ مجھے اس کے آدھے کے عوض فلوس اور آدھے کے عوض ایک حبہ کم نصف درہم دے دے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک فلوس میں یہ بیع جائز ہے اور مابقیہ میں باطل ہے کیونکہ فلوس کے عوض نصف درہم کی بیع تو جائز ہے اور نصف درہم کی بیع حبہ کم نصف درہم کے عوض ربوا ہے اسلئے ناجائز ہے اور ابوحنیفہ کے قول کے مطابق کل میں بیع باطل ہے کیونکہ صفقہ متحد اور فساد قوی ہے۔ اسلئے فساد پھیل جائے گا اور اس کی نظیر گذر چکی ہے۔ اور اگر لفظ اعطاء مکرر کیا ہو تو امام صاحب کا حکم صاحبین کے حکم کے مانند ہوگا۔ یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ دو عقد ہیں اور اگر کہا کہ مجھے نصف درہم فلوس اور حبہ کم نصف درہم دے دے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اس نے درہم کا مقابلہ ان فلوس کے ساتھ کیا جو نصف درہم کے عوض بکتے ہیں اور حبہ کم نصف درہم کے ساتھ کیا۔ پس حبہ کم نصف درہم اسکے مثل کے عوض ہو گا۔ اور اسکے علاوہ فلوس کے مقابلہ میں ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کے اکثر نسخوں میں دوسرا مسئلہ مذکور ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں تین مسئلے مذکور ہیں۔ پہلا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے صراف کو ایک درہم دے کر کہا کہ تو مجھے اس کے نصف
He gave a dirham to a money-changer and said, 'Give me for half of it fulus and for the other half half a dirham minus one grain.' The sale is valid in the fulus and void in the remainder according to them (Sahibayn), because the sale of half a dirham for fulus is valid, but the sale of half a dirham for half a dirham minus a grain is riba and therefore invalid. And on the analogy of the saying of Abu Hanifa, it is void in all, because the transaction is unitary and the corruption is strong, so it spreads. And its like has passed. And if he repeated the word of giving (a'ta), then his ruling is like their ruling; that is correct because they are two sales. And if he said, 'Give me half a dirham of fulus and half a dirham minus a grain', it is valid, because he matched the dirham with the fulus which are sold for half a dirham and with half a dirham minus a grain. So half a dirham minus a grain is for its like, and the surplus is for the fulus. The author of al-Hidayah said: In most copies of al-Mukhtasar, the second mas'ala is mentioned. Explanation: In this phrase, three mas'ala are mentioned. The first mas'ala is that a person gave a money-changer a dirham and said, 'Give me for half of it...' (incomplete). Translation: And if someone gave a money-changer a dirham and said, 'Give me for half of it fulus and for the other half half a dirham minus one grain', then according to the Sahibayn, this sale is valid in the fulus and void in the remainder, because the sale of half a dirham for fulus is valid, and the sale of half a dirham for half a dirham minus a grain is riba, so it is invalid. And according to the saying of Abu Hanifa, the entire sale is void, because the transaction is unitary and the corruption is strong, so it spreads. And its example has passed. And if the word of giving is repeated, then the ruling of Imam (Abu Hanifa) is like the ruling of the Sahibayn. This is correct because they are two contracts. And if he said, 'Give me half a dirham of fulus and half a dirham minus a grain', then it is valid, because he matched the dirham with the fulus that are sold for half a dirham and with half a dirham minus a grain. Thus half a dirham minus a grain is for its like, and what remains is for the fulus. The author of Hidayah says: In most copies of al-Mukhtasar, the second mas'ala is mentioned. Explanation: In this phrase, three mas'ala are mentioned. The first mas'ala is that a person gave a money-changer a dirham and said, 'Give me for half of it...'
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a compound transaction involving riba. The scenario: a person gives a money-changer one dirham and asks for two things: (1) fulus worth half a dirham, and (2) half a dirham minus one grain (a small unit). The second request involves exchanging half a dirham for a slightly smaller amount of silver (half dirham minus a grain), which is riba al-fadl (unequal exchange of the same genus). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that the sale of fulus (for half dirham) is valid, but the exchange of half dirham with a deficiency is riba and void. Since the transaction is composite, only the invalid part is void. Abu Hanifa, however, rules the entire transaction void because the contract is one (safqah wahidah) and the corruption is strong, thus it spreads to the whole. The text then adds: if the word 'a'ta' (give) is repeated (i.e., two separate requests), then Abu Hanifa agrees with the Sahibayn because it becomes two distinct contracts. Finally, if the request is simply 'give me half a dirham of fulus and half a dirham minus a grain' (without specifying halves of the dirham), it is valid because the entire dirham is matched against the fulus and the silver amount; the half dirham minus a grain is exchanged for its like (a valid exchange of equal silver amounts, but here the difference is counted as part of the fulus price). The commentary (تشريح) begins to list three mas'ala but is cut off. This passage illustrates the Hanafi principle that a single contract with both valid and invalid parts is treated as void by Abu Hanifa if the invalid part is strong (riba), while the Sahibayn split the contract. It also shows the effect of repetition of the offer.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Exchange of money; the chapter deals with currency exchange rules including riba.
ربو (riba): Usury; in this passage, riba al-fadl (excess in exchange of same genus, here silver for silver).
صفقة (safqah): The transaction or bargain; considered 'unitary' (muttahid) when made in one contract.
حبہ (habbah): A grain; a small unit of weight, used here to create a deficiency in exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person gives a dirham to a money-changer and says 'Give me for half of this dirham fulus and for the other half half a dirham minus one grain', what is the ruling of Abu Hanifa?
A) The entire transaction is valid because the fulus part is valid.
B) The entire transaction is void because the contract is one and riba spreads.
C) The fulus part is valid and the silver exchange is void.
D) It is valid only if the money-changer separates the two requests.

Key Takeaway
In a composite transaction with riba, the unity of the contract determines whether the corruption spreads: if the contract is one, Abu Hanifa voids all; if split into separate offers, only the riba part is void.
